class="Layout-Section"><div id="iiris-identity" data-testid="iris-identity"></div><div data-template="article" class="undefined ArticleBase"><div class="TwoColumnLayout"><div class="ArticleBase-HeaderTitle"><noscript><span class="ArticleBase-LargeTitle">China's hectic AI rollout has left data centers idling</span></noscript><span class="ArticleBase-LargeTitle" data-testid="article-title">China's hectic AI rollout has left data centers idling</span><span class="ArticleBase-DefaultTitle" data-testid="article-default-title">China's hectic AI rollout has left data centers idling</span></h1><p class="ArticleBase-HeaderSummary" data-testid="article-summary">Poorly designed AI data centers struggle to provide advanced services.</p></div></div></div><div class="TwoColumnLayout-Content"><div class="TwoColumnLayout-Body"><div class="ArticleBase-Body" data-testid="article-base-body"><div class="ArticleBase-Contributors" class="SocialShare-IconWrapper SocialShare-IconWrapper_variant_button"><span data-component="icon" data-name="Twitter" class="SocialShare-Icon SocialShare-Icon_variant_button SocialShare-Icon_type_twitter" class="ArticleBase-BodyContent ArticleBase-BodyContent_Article" data-testid="article-base-body-content"><div data-module="content" class="ContentModule-Wrapper"><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">China&#x27;s plunge into AI has created a huge amount of excess data center capacity.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">According to investigations by Chinese media, data center players have built too much capacity, lack the skills to carry out complex AI processes, and have overestimated demand.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">China is</span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20250730210846/https://www.premia-partners.com/insight/china-s-east-data-west-computing-initiative-power-infrastructure-as-the-next-big-thing-in-the-global-ai-race"> planning to establish</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> 50 intelligent computing centers by 2025, increasing its computing capacity by a third over four years – although according to one estimate, 70 new centers are already under construction.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">In contrast to CPU-based legacy data centers, AI data centers integrate GPU and other types of chips for simultaneous processing of huge workloads. They consume as much as four times the energy of traditional data centers.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">A</span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20250730210846/https://mp.weixin.qq.com/s/BoNXsXTmdgTBABZATQTyow?utm_source=substack&amp;utm_medium=email"> report</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> by AI Technology Review late last year complained the market had &quot;blindly advanced&quot; data center construction and had over-estimated demand, resulting in idle servers and in some cases the closure of intelligent computing centers.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">It estimated an intelligent data center with 1,250 servers supporting large model training and inference could cost up to 1 billion Chinese yuan (US$141 million) a year to run, mostly in power costs and depreciation.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><span class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_bold">Storage, not compute</span></span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">A big part of China&#x27;s push into high-powered computing has been its East-West Computing Initiative, in which data generated in the high-income cities of the east can be processed by data centers in western provinces, taking advantage of low costs, clean energy and cheap land.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">That was the plan, but the reality is that many of these western China facilities are operating at well under capacity, according to an</span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20250730210846/http://big5.xinhuanet.com/gate/big5/www.gz.xinhuanet.com/20240115/485648f473094610ba8e1967651a4cc8/c.html"> investigation published by the official Xinhua</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link ContentText-BodyTextChunk_italic" target="_blank" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20250730210846/http://big5.xinhuanet.com/gate/big5/www.gz.xinhuanet.com/20240115/485648f473094610ba8e1967651a4cc8/c.html"> </a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20250730210846/http://big5.xinhuanet.com/gate/big5/www.gz.xinhuanet.com/20240115/485648f473094610ba8e1967651a4cc8/c.html">news agency</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">Demand from eastern seaboard customers for data services in the west was weak, with relatively few mature commercial applications, the study found. Instead of providing compute services, the main use case in the western China facilities was storage.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">The new data centers are unable to support customers with low latency and complex processing requirements. </span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">Interviewees also blamed high network charges, with a 1Gbit/s dedicated line costing RMB160,000 ($22,500) a month, eliminating the advantages of the lower rental and power costs.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">Another problem is the poorly architected AI data centers, which require intricate coordination across compute, storage and networking.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">Sha Kaibo, a vice president of Tencent Cloud,</span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20250730210846/https://mp.weixin.qq.com/s/P4gfJuB3DbhCLE7H6SBYyA?utm_source=substack&amp;utm_medium=email"> compared it to buying a premium sports car</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> but not understanding its advanced features and lacking a professional team to maintain it, with the result that &quot;you can only drive it on ordinary roads.&quot;</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">This is not a problem confined to data centers. China&#x27;s</span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"><a class="ContentText-BodyTextChunk ContentText-BodyTextChunk_link" target="_blank" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20250730210846/https://www.scmp.com/business/china-business/article/3277461/chinas-trillion-yuan-emerging-energy-storage-market-already-turmoil?module=feature_package_2&amp;pgtype=homepage"> energy storage market</a></span><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text"> is another case in point, also suffering from over-capacity and low usage.</span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">Of course, the rest of the world is greatly exercised about China&#x27;s over-invested manufacturing sector and whether it plans to dump its surplus abroad. </span></p><p class="ContentParagraph ContentParagraph_align_left" data-testid="content-paragraph"><span class="ContentText ContentText_variant_bodyNormal" data-testid="content-text">The underlying issue is that over-capacity is endemic in the top-down economic system. The central government identifies priority sectors in which it offers easy credit and handouts, attracting eager enterprises and local governments with little regard for market conditions.</span></p></div></div><div class="ArticleBase-More" data-testid="article-base-more"><p class="ArticleBase-MoreTitle">Read more about:</p><a data-component="keyword" class="Keyword Keyword_variant_category-2 Keyword_title_ai ArticleBase-Keywords" href="/web/20250730210846/https://www.lightreading.com/keyword/ai" data-discover="true">AI</a><a data-component="keyword" class="Keyword Keyword_variant_category-2 Keyword_title_asia ArticleBase-Keywords" href="/web/20250730210846/https://www.lightreading.com/keyword/asia" data-discover="true">Asia</a></div><div logo imprinted on a chipset\",\"Featured Story\",\"heading\",\"Europe's love of Huawei is crushing Ericsson and Nokia\",\"mobileHeading\",\"articleBody\",[1372,1377,1382,1395,1406,1413,1418,1423,1428,1441,1446,1451,1456,1461,1466,1471,1476,1481,1486,1491,1496,1501,1506,1511],{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1373,\"_976\":1374},{\"_974\":975},[1375],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1376},\"Ursula von der Leyen, the European Commission's president, had sounded as firm and unyielding as her immaculately sculpted hair looked in the hours after Donald Trump's April Liberation Day, when the US president launched a salvo of tariffs against US friends and foes alike. The European Union (EU) had \\\"a strong plan to retaliate,\\\" she proclaimed. But when a US-EU trade deal was concluded on July 27, it included little to make Europeans happy – a punishing 15% tariff on EU goods (with some important exemptions) and a promise to invest hundreds of billions in US energy, military and technology goods.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1378,\"_976\":1379},{\"_974\":975},[1380],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1381},\"Von der Layen was not, as a condition of the deal, even required to do more about Huawei's infiltration of Europe's telecom networks, one that critics say has weakened both Ericsson and Nokia, the EU-based alternatives. There was outrage from EU and US quarters last week after Spain signed a piddly 12 million euro (US$14 million) contract to use the Chinese company's hardware for storage of state wiretaps. Yet there has recently been silence about the much grander sums Huawei earns from its 5G deals with numerous European telcos. Indeed, parts of the mainstream media seem to have forgotten about the heavy reliance of some countries on Huawei's technology – or even to think mistakenly it has been banished.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1383,\"_976\":1384},{\"_974\":975},[1385,1387,1393],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1386},\"The EU's biggest economy has certainly done a good job of hoodwinking the press and Huawei's opponents. One year ago, \",{\"_211\":979,\"_1066\":1388,\"_979\":1392},[1389],{\"_211\":299,\"_972\":1390},{\"_5\":1391,\"_1071\":1072,\"_1073\":-5,\"_1074\":-5},\"https://www.bmi.bund.de/SharedDocs/pressemitteilungen/EN/2024/07/5g-en.html\",\"Germany published a statement\",{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1394},\" ordering its telcos to ensure the 5G core, the control center of the network, was free of components built by Huawei or ZTE, another Chinese vendor, before the end of 2026.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1396,\"_976\":1397},{\"_974\":975},[1398,1400,1404],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1399},\"Telcos were also told to replace the \\\"critical management systems\\\" of Huawei and ZTE in their 5G access and transport networks by the end of 2029. In her otherwise excellent book \",{\"_211\":979,\"_1066\":1401,\"_979\":1403},[1402],{\"_211\":1134},\"House of Huawei\",{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1405},\", Washington Post reporter Eva Dou wrongly interpreted this by writing: \\\"In July 2024, Germany's government announced that its major telecom companies would stop using Huawei and ZTE 5G equipment within five years, a big victory for Washington.\\\"\",{\"_211\":1367,\"_972\":1407,\"_976\":1410},{\"_974\":975,\"_1408\":1409},\"level\",5,[1411],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1412},\"The G of living dangerously\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1414,\"_976\":1415},{\"_974\":975},[1416],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1417},\"What Germany's government had actually done was cook up an arrangement with the country's Huawei-using operators, allowing them to retain the bulk of its products. At the time of the announcement, none of the operators was still using Huawei or ZTE in its 5G core, meaning that rule had no practical value. Elsewhere, it is only configuration management, a small part of the system, that operators must replace, according to telco sources. They still have four and a half years to do it and will not have to extract Huawei's basestations and basestation software if they can pull it off. Were it so inclined, Huawei could just as easily use that basestation software as it could the management system for nefarious purposes, say experts, although there has never been any firm evidence of such wrongdoing by Huawei.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1419,\"_976\":1420},{\"_974\":975},[1421],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1422},\"Fear of Huawei as a Chinese government stooge, able to spy on European citizens or cripple communications, is the ostensible reason for the EU campaign against it. Yet Germany has done almost nothing to minimize its reliance on Huawei's 5G technology. In a groundbreaking report in 2020, Strand Consult, a Danish analyst company, calculated that Huawei was present at 57% of Germany's 4G sites in 2019. Last year, it put Huawei's share of the country's 5G sites at an even higher 59%. Deutsche Telekom and Vodafone, two of Germany's three big mobile telcos, each counts Huawei as its main radio access network vendor. Telefónica, the other, divides work between Huawei and Nokia.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1424,\"_976\":1425},{\"_974\":975},[1426],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1427},\"Other countries appear to be taking their lead from Germany and eyeing its plan/fudge (delete, according to bias) with interest. Of 31 European countries inside and outside the EU that have launched 5G services, only six were not using Huawei at all last year, while 15 were reliant on it for more than a third of 5G sites, according to Strand Consult's data. That illustrates a disregard for the \\\"5G toolbox,\\\" the EU's pamphlet about the dangers so-called \\\"high-risk vendors\\\" pose in 5G networks.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1429,\"_976\":1430},{\"_974\":975},[1431,1433,1439],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1432},\"\\\"I am very concerned about the fact that a significant number of the 5G sites across EU member states are still provided by high-risk suppliers,\\\" said Henna Virkkunen, the European Commission's vice president for tech sovereignty, \",{\"_211\":979,\"_1066\":1434,\"_979\":1438},[1435],{\"_211\":299,\"_972\":1436},{\"_5\":1437,\"_1071\":1072,\"_1073\":-5,\"_1074\":-5},\"https://www.lightreading.com/5g/europe-threatens-further-measures-against-huawei-as-trump-returns\",\"at the start of the year\",{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1440},\". \\\"This has a potentially serious negative impact on security for end users and companies and to our critical infrastructure.\\\"\",{\"_211\":1367,\"_972\":1442,\"_976\":1443},{\"_974\":975,\"_1408\":1409},[1444],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1445},\"Scandi noir\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1447,\"_976\":1448},{\"_974\":975},[1449],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1450},\"The refusal to evict Huawei frustrates the bosses of Ericsson and Nokia, the Nordic vendors that would most obviously benefit from it. Börje Ekholm, Ericsson's CEO, was critical of the Swedish government's decision to ban Huawei from its 5G network in late 2020. That was probably because he feared Chinese reprisals would hurt Ericsson, whose China revenues fell 46% in 2021. More recently, however, Ekholm has grumbled about the probability of losing market share in some parts of the world to aggressive Chinese rivals. Earlier this month, he sounded doubtful that new opportunities to replace high-risk vendors in Europe would ever materialize.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1452,\"_976\":1453},{\"_974\":975},[1454],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1455},\"But Justin Hotard, who succeeded Pekka Lundmark as Nokia's CEO in April, struck a more optimistic tone last week. \\\"I think that's significant,\\\" he said on a call with reporters, referring to Virkkunen's desire to clamp down on high-risk vendors. \\\"We see that as an opportunity for us given our market position.\\\"\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1457,\"_976\":1458},{\"_974\":975},[1459],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1460},\"Nokia did, notably, land a contract last November to replace Huawei at about 3,000 of Deutsche Telekom's 5G sites in Germany – roughly 8% of the RAN total, according to data the operator included in its capital markets day presentations last year. The deal was a long time in the making and is curious given that Deutsche Telekom opposes efforts to evict Huawei. But the introduction of a third RAN vendor could seem prudent. German authorities, under mounting domestic, EU and US pressure, might always decide on a tougher approach, as the UK previously did.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1462,\"_976\":1463},{\"_974\":975},[1464],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1465},\"The longer they and other countries resist, the worse things could be for Ericsson and Nokia. RAN sales flattened year-over-year in the first quarter of 2025, after steep drops in 2023 and 2024 that lowered annual revenues last year by more than a fifth, to about $35 billion, compared with the figure in 2022, according to the analyst company Omdia. This year, Omdia expects \\\"low single-digit percentage growth.\\\" But market share gains would put the Nordic companies in a much healthier position, and meaningful gains could only come at Huawei's expense, unless Ericsson and Nokia were trampling over each other's turf.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1467,\"_976\":1468},{\"_974\":975},[1469],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1470},\"That has certainly happened and is the main reason for Nokia's predicament in the US, where it is being replaced by Ericsson across one third of the AT\u0026T network. Omdia's data shows Nokia's global RAN market share fell from 19.5% in 2023 to 17.6% last year, just as Ericsson's grew from 24.3% to 25.7%. After the loss of Verizon as a mobile customer several years ago, Nokia's only big remaining RAN client in the US is T-Mobile.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1472,\"_976\":1473},{\"_974\":975},[1474],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1475},\"The setbacks in such a big and relatively profitable market have torn into sales and profit margins at Nokia's mobile networks business group. Its second quarter revenues fell by almost €700 million ($815 million) between 2020 and 2025, to around €1.7 billion ($2 billion), and its operating margin for the recent quarter was just 4.4%, half as much as a year before.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1477,\"_976\":1478},{\"_974\":975},[1479],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1480},\"Job cuts shrank the size of the Nokia workforce from about 86,700 employees in 2023 to 75,600 last December, and the axe has fallen heavily on mobile. In a restructuring that harks back to an earlier era and could precipitate further cuts, Nokia is moving several corporate functions outside individual units and into a group-wide layer. Additional cuts within mobile would now be hard to realize without hurting critical research and development activities.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1482,\"_976\":1483},{\"_974\":975},[1484],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1485},\"Ericsson, while in stronger RAN shape, is also fighting market stagnation made worse by US tariffs and the weakness of the US dollar. It looks unhealthily reliant on American business, generating 44% of its second quarter revenues in the US. Work in India has seemingly dried up, following a frenzied deployment of 5G networks, and China revenues fell by 37% year-over-year for the recent second quarter, to about 2.2 billion Swedish kronor ($230 million). To protect margins, Ekholm cut about 6,000 jobs last year, or 6% of the total.\",{\"_211\":1367,\"_972\":1487,\"_976\":1488},{\"_974\":975,\"_1408\":1409},[1489],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1490},\"The longest running tender in history\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1492,\"_976\":1493},{\"_974\":975},[1494],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1495},\"Much like Deutsche Telekom, major European telco groups like Vodafone have resisted government attempts to ban Huawei, which continues to be admired by technology executives for its 5G smarts. An initial concern was that a shortage of 5G suppliers would leave operators facing a Nordic duopoly if Huawei were banned. What's more, Nokia's first wave of 5G offers did not look competitive after product blunders and the distraction of the €15.6 billion ($18.1 billion, at today's exchange rate) Alcatel-Lucent takeover in 2016.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1497,\"_976\":1498},{\"_974\":975},[1499],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1500},\"Today, this seems like ancient history. For all its financial problems, Nokia's 5G business is technologically on much more solid ground. The emergence of South Korea's Samsung as a viable 5G option, proven by its vaunted contract with Verizon in the US, should also have addressed concerns about a Nordic duopoly or Ericsson monopoly.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1502,\"_976\":1503},{\"_974\":975},[1504],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1505},\"Yet telcos, having not profited from 5G, are in no mood for early Huawei swap-outs that would gobble funds. The biggest opportunity for other vendors seemed to be a Vodafone RAN tender encompassing 170,000 basestation sites across Europe and Africa, according to the operator's annual report last year. But Vodafone's sale of businesses in Hungary, Italy and Spain, and the exclusion from the tender of joint network ventures in the UK and the Netherlands, are likely to have dramatically lowered that number.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1507,\"_976\":1508},{\"_974\":975},[1509],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1510},\"The tender finished and its results were shared with participants early this year, according to multiple sources, and yet Vodafone has provided no public update on the outcome. It makes no mention of the process in this year's annual report, published as recently as last month. In its last set of results, however, Vodafone said it had no plans to raise capital intensity – spending as a percentage of revenues – above the recent historic level, which was 18% in its last fiscal year.\",{\"_211\":971,\"_972\":1512,\"_976\":1513},{\"_974\":975},[1514],{\"_211\":979,\"_979\":1515},\"Whether or not Huawei deserves its EU and US blacklisting, the danger is that Europe's continued reliance on it further weakens Nokia's mobile networks business. Added to Europe's other negatives, it could ultimately persuade Ericsson to follow the journey of the similarly named Leif Erikson, the Viking thought to have sailed to America more than 1,000 years ago. A relocation of headquarters from Sweden to the US was threatened by Ekholm last year. For a region increasingly short of big companies with global influence, that would surely be a disaster.\",\"The unwillingness of European governments and telcos to evict Huawei, now deemed a security threat by the European Commission, is worsening the pain felt by Ericsson and Nokia.\",\"body\",\"callToAction\",{\"_979\":1520,\"_178\":1521},\"More\",\"/5g/europe-s-love-of-huawei-is-crushing-ericsson-and-nokia\",{},\"2025-07-29T07:30:00.000Z\",{\"_1264\":139,\"_1265\":1525},[],\"relatedEvents\",[],\"topicSelector\",{\"_1530\":1531,\"_1533\":944},\"mainTopic\",{\"_211\":946,\"_232\":443,\"_178\":444,\"_947\":1532},{\"_211\":949,\"_232\":439},\"additionalTopics\",\"disclaimer\",[],{\"_1537\":139,\"_1538\":1539},\"isPaidContent\",\"paidProductTaxonomies\",[],\"errorModal\",{\"_1542\":139,\"_1543\":1544,\"_1545\":1546},\"showErrorModal\",\"errorTitle\",\"Oops!
